</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Rice dish</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about a dish. For the country, see <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>. For the <i>Dragon Ball</i> character, see <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Pilaf" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Pilaf">Emperor Pilaf</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Fried_rice" title="Fried rice">Fried rice</a>.</div>

.sister-inline-image img[src*="Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg"]{filter:invert(1)brightness(55%)contrast(250%)hue-rotate(180deg)}}</style><span class="noviewer sister-inline-image" typeof="mw:File"><a href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Cookbook:Rice_Pilaf" class="extiw" title="b:Cookbook:Rice Pilaf">Cookbook: Pilaf</a></li><li>&#160;<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Pilaf" class="extiw" title="commons:Category:Pilaf">Media&#58; Pilaf</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Pilaf</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small"><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </span><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span></span>/</a></span></span>), <b>pilav</b> or <b>pilau</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991" /><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small"><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </span><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/aʊ/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">aʊ</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;p&#39; in &#39;pie&#39;">p</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/aʊ/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">aʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> dish, or in some regions, a wheat dish, whose recipe usually involves cooking in <a href="/wiki/Stock_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock (cooking)">stock</a> or <a href="/wiki/Broth" title="Broth">broth</a>, adding spices, and other ingredients such as vegetables, meat, or chicken,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-pilauOED&#95;2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pilauOED-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEMerriam-Webster&#95;Unabridged&#95;Dictionary2019&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMerriam-Webster_Unabridged_Dictionary2019-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and employing some technique for achieving cooked grains that do not adhere.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEPerry2014624&#95;6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerry2014624-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoger20001144&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoger20001144-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a>, such methods of cooking rice at first spread through a vast territory  from <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and eventually to a wider world. The Spanish <i><a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">paella</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoger20001143&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoger20001143-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the South Asian <i>pilau</i> or <i>pulao</i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTENandy200411&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENandy200411-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Nandy11&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nandy11-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Biryani" title="Biryani">biryani</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESengupta201474&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESengupta201474-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sengupta74&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sengupta74-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> evolved from such dishes.
</p><p>Pilaf and similar dishes are common to <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_cuisine" title="Middle Eastern cuisine">Middle Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balkan_cuisine" title="Balkan cuisine">Balkan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_cuisine" title="Caribbean cuisine">Caribbean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasian cuisine">South Caucasian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_cuisine" title="Central Asian cuisine">Central Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_African_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="East African cuisine">East African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_European_cuisine" title="Eastern European cuisine">Eastern European</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_cuisine" title="Latin American cuisine">Latin American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">Maritime Southeast Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_cuisine" title="South Asian cuisine">South Asian</a> cuisines; in these areas, they are regarded as <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple dishes</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Marks&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marks-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Cavendish&#95;18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-StreetFood&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StreetFood-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i> Online Edition's summary, the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> word <i>pilaf</i>, which the OED, refers to the version with spelling "pilau," is a borrowing partly from <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, partly from <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, and partly also from <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>. In more detail, the English pilau, of first use 1609 CE, has come from Persian pulaw (16th cent. as palāv), in turn from <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> pulāv dish of rice and meat, from <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> pulāka ball of rice, probably from <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian</a> (cf <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> puḷukku (adjective) simmered, (noun) boiled or parboiled food, puḷukkal cooked rice); probably partly via <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> pilau (1654; 1680 as pilaw; 1833 as pilaf), <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> pilao (1542).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Arroz_enjoyado_-_Morasa_Pol%C3%B3.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Arroz_enjoyado_-_Morasa_Pol%C3%B3.JPG/250px-Arroz_enjoyado_-_Morasa_Pol%C3%B3.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Arroz_enjoyado_-_Morasa_Pol%C3%B3.JPG/500px-Arroz_enjoyado_-_Morasa_Pol%C3%B3.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>Persian Pollo</figcaption></figure>
<p>Although the cultivation of rice had spread much earlier from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> to <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asia</a>, it was at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a> that methods of cooking rice which approximate modern styles of cooking pilaf at first spread through a vast territory from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> to <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, and eventually to a wider world. The Spanish <i><a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">paella</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTERoger20001143&#95;10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoger20001143-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> <i>pilau</i> or <i>pulao</i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTENandy200411&#95;12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENandy200411-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Biryani" title="Biryani">biryani</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTESengupta201474&#95;14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESengupta201474-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> evolved from such dishes.
</p><p>According to author <a href="/wiki/K._T._Achaya" title="K. T. Achaya">K. T. Achaya</a>, the Indian epic <i><a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a></i> mentions an instance of rice and meat cooked together. Also, according to Achaya, "pulao" or "pallao" is used to refer to a rice dish in ancient Sanskrit works such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Y%C4%81j%C3%B1avalkya_Sm%E1%B9%9Bti" title="Yājñavalkya Smṛti">Yājñavalkya Smṛti</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-KTAchaya1994&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KTAchaya1994-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, according to food writers <a href="/wiki/Colleen_Taylor_Sen" title="Colleen Taylor Sen">Colleen Taylor Sen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Perry_(food_writer)" title="Charles Perry (food writer)">Charles Perry</a>, and social theorist <a href="/wiki/Ashis_Nandy" title="Ashis Nandy">Ashis Nandy</a>, these references do not substantially correlate to the commonly used meaning and history implied in pilafs, which appear in Indian accounts after the medieval Central Asian conquests.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> and his army, many centuries earlier, in the 4th century BCE, have been reported to have been so impressed with the Eastern Iranian <a href="/wiki/Bactria" title="Bactria">Bactrian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sogdia" title="Sogdia">Sogdian</a> <i>pilavs</i> that his soldiers brought the recipes back to <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Macedonia</a> when they returned.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nabhan&#95;29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nabhan-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similar stories exist of Alexander bringing pilaf to the ancient Persian <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>; however, they are considered apocryphal by art historian <a href="/wiki/John_Boardman_(art_historian)" title="John Boardman (art historian)">John Boardman</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEBoardman2019102&#95;30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoardman2019102-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly, it has been reported that pilaf was consumed in the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest documented recipe for pilaf comes from the tenth-century <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persian</a> scholar <a href="/wiki/Avicenna" title="Avicenna">Avicenna</a> (Ibn Sīnā), who in his books on medical sciences dedicated a whole section to preparing various dishes, including several types of pilaf. In doing so, he described the advantages and disadvantages of every item used for preparing the dish. Accordingly, Persians consider Avicenna to be the "father" of modern pilaf.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-nabhan&#95;29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nabhan-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>Thirteenth-century texts describe the consistency of pilaf that the grains should be plump and somewhat firm to resemble peppercorns with no mushiness, and each grain should be separate with no clumping.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guardian&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Another primary source for pilaf dishes comes from the 17th-century Iranian philosopher <a href="/wiki/Molla_Sadra" class="mw-redirect" title="Molla Sadra">Molla Sadra</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-algar&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-algar-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Persian Pilau became the standard fare in West Asia and <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> over the years.
</p><p>During the period of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, the Central Asian versions of the dish spread throughout all Soviet republics, becoming a part of the common <a href="/wiki/Soviet_cuisine" title="Soviet cuisine">Soviet cuisine</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Preparation">Preparation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Preparation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Some cooks prefer to use <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">basmati</a> rice because it is easier to prepare a pilaf where the grains stay "light, fluffy and separate" with this type of rice. However, other types of long-grain rice are also used. The rice is rinsed thoroughly before use to remove the surface starch. Pilaf can be cooked in water or stock. Common additions include fried onions and fragrant spices like <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_leaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay leaves">bay leaves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guardian&#95;32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Pilaf is usually made with meat or vegetables, but it can also be made plain which is called <i>sade pilav</i> in <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>, <i>chelo</i> in <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> and <i>ruzz mufalfal</i> in <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson2014624&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson2014624-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Persian pilaf uses <a href="/wiki/Saffron" title="Saffron">saffron</a> which gives Persian rice its unique yellow color and taste. Pilaf is often made by adding the rice to hot fat and stirring briefly before adding the cooking liquid. The fat used varies from recipe to recipe. Cooking methods vary with respect to details such as pre-soaking the rice and steaming after boiling.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guardian&#95;32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Local_varieties">Local varieties</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Local varieties"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>There are thousands of variations of pilaf made with rice or other grains like <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">bulgur</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guardian&#95;32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>Some include different combinations of meats, fruits or vegetables, while others are simple and served plain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-guardian&#95;32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_cuisine" title="Central Asian cuisine">Central Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_cuisine" title="South Asian cuisine">South Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iranian_cuisine" title="Iranian cuisine">Iranian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_cuisine" title="Caribbean cuisine">Caribbean cuisine</a> are some with distinctive styles of making pilaf.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-perry&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perry-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Afghanistan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Bukhari_Meal_-_Pilaf.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bukhari_Meal_-_Pilaf.jpg/250px-Bukhari_Meal_-_Pilaf.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="333" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bukhari_Meal_-_Pilaf.jpg/500px-Bukhari_Meal_-_Pilaf.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a><figcaption>Bukhari (pilaf) meal in Saudi Arabia</figcaption></figure>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Afghan_cuisine" title="Afghan cuisine">Afghan cuisine</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kabuli_palaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabuli palaw">Kabuli palaw</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>: <span lang="fa" dir="rtl">کابلی پلو</span>) is made by cooking <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">basmati</a> with mutton, lamb, beef or chicken, and oil. Kabuli palaw is cooked in large shallow and thick dishes. Fried sliced <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrots</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raisin" title="Raisin">raisins</a> are added. Chopped nuts like <a href="/wiki/Pistachio" title="Pistachio">pistachios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walnut" title="Walnut">walnuts</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Almond" title="Almond">almonds</a> may be added as well. The meat is covered by the rice or buried in the middle of the dish. Kabuli palaw rice with carrots and raisins is very popular in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, where it is known as <i>roz Bukhari</i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">رز بخاري</span>), meaning '<a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Bukharan</a> rice'.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Albania">Albania</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Albania"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Albanian_cuisine" title="Albanian cuisine">Albanian cuisine</a>, pilaf is a very common dish.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RiceConsumptionInEurope&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiceConsumptionInEurope-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is typically accompanied by yogurt and eaten with bean stew, meat soup or baked meats such as chicken and lamb. Medium-long grain rice is used, and it is cooked plainly with butter, resulting in a soft yet non-sticky texture.
</p><p>There are various rice dishes in Albania, which are all commonly referred to as pilaf.
</p><p>Albania ranks among the top three countries in Europe for rice consumption.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RiceConsumptionInEurope&#95;36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiceConsumptionInEurope-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Armenia">Armenia</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Armenia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Chou_farci-Arm%C3%A9nie.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Chou_farci-Arm%C3%A9nie.jpg/250px-Chou_farci-Arm%C3%A9nie.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Chou_farci-Arm%C3%A9nie.jpg/500px-Chou_farci-Arm%C3%A9nie.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a><figcaption>Armenian <a href="/wiki/Cabbage_roll" title="Cabbage roll">cabbage roll</a> stuffed with chickpeas and bulgur pilaf</figcaption></figure>
<p>Armenians use a lot of <i><a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">bulgur</a></i> ("cracked wheat") in their pilaf dishes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Armenian recipes may combine <a href="/wiki/Vermicelli" title="Vermicelli">vermicelli</a> or <a href="/wiki/Orzo" title="Orzo">orzo</a> with rice cooked in stock seasoned with mint, parsley and allspice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One traditional Armenian pilaf is made with the same noodle rice mixture cooked in stock with <a href="/wiki/Raisins" class="mw-redirect" title="Raisins">raisins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Almonds">almonds</a> and allspice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Armenian kinds of rice are discussed by Rose Baboian in her cookbook from 1964 which includes recipes for different pilafs, most rooted in her birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Antep" class="mw-redirect" title="Antep">Antep</a> in Turkey.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Baboian recommends that the noodles be stir-fried first in chicken fat before being added to the pilaf. Another Armenian cookbook written by Vağinag Pürad recommends to render poultry fat in the oven with red pepper until the fat mixture turns a red color before using the strained fat to prepare pilaf.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><i>Lapa</i> is an Armenian word with several meanings one of which is a "watery boiled rice, thick rice soup, mush" and <i>lepe</i> which refers to various rice dishes differing by region.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Antranig Azhderian describes Armenian pilaf as a "dish resembling porridge".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Azerbaijan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Azerbaijani cuisine includes more than 40 different plov recipes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-kukhnya&#95;44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kukhnya-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One of the most reputed dishes is plov from saffron-covered rice, served with various herbs and greens, a combination distinctive from Central Asian pilaf. Traditional Azerbaijani plov consists of three distinct components, served simultaneously but on separate platters: rice (warm, never hot), <i>gara</i> (fried beef or chicken pieces with onion, chestnut and dried fruits prepared as an accompaniment to rice), and herbs. Gara is put on the rice when eating plov, but it is never mixed with rice and the other components. Pilaf is often called aş in Azerbaijani cuisine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-mamedov&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mamedov-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="center gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
	<li class="gallerycaption">Rice pilaf examples from Azerbaijan</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 210px; height: 175px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG" class="mw-file-description" title="Azerbaijani plov with qazmaq (the same as Persian tahdig), served with choban salad"><img alt="Azerbaijani plov with qazmaq (the same as Persian tahdig), served with choban salad" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG/250px-A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG/330px-A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG/500px-A%C5%9F_v%C9%99_salat.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2889" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext"><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_cuisine" title="Azerbaijani cuisine">Azerbaijani</a> plov with <i>qazmaq</i> (the same as Persian <i><a href="/wiki/Tahdig" class="mw-redirect" title="Tahdig">tahdig</a></i>), served with <a href="/wiki/Choban_salad" class="mw-redirect" title="Choban salad">choban salad</a></div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 210px; height: 175px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Shah-plow_azerbaijani.JPG" class="mw-file-description" title="Azerbaijani shah-pilaf"><img alt="Azerbaijani shah-pilaf" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Shah-plow_azerbaijani.JPG/250px-Shah-plow_azerbaijani.JPG" decoding="async" width="145" height="145" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Shah-plow_azerbaijani.JPG/330px-Shah-plow_azerbaijani.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2706" data-file-height="2700" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext"><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_cuisine" title="Azerbaijani cuisine">Azerbaijani</a> shah-pilaf</div>
		</li>
</ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Bangladesh"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshi_cuisine" title="Bangladeshi cuisine">Bangladeshi cuisine</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%E0%A6%AE%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B0%E0%A6%97_%E0%A6%AA%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%93_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%E0%A6%AE%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B0%E0%A6%97_%E0%A6%AA%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%93_2.jpg/250px-%E0%A6%AE%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B0%E0%A6%97_%E0%A6%AA%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%93_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="256" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/%E0%A6%AE%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B0%E0%A6%97_%E0%A6%AA%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%93_2.jpg/500px-%E0%A6%AE%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B0%E0%A6%97_%E0%A6%AA%E0%A7%8B%E0%A6%B2%E0%A6%BE%E0%A6%93_2.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1997" data-file-height="2048" /></a><figcaption>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Old_Dhaka" title="Old Dhaka">Old Dhaka</a> style chicken pilaf, locally known as <i>Murog Polao</i></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Traditional_Holiday_Lunch_of_Bangladesh(_Polao_Korma_ilish_vaja,kabab).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Traditional_Holiday_Lunch_of_Bangladesh%28_Polao_Korma_ilish_vaja%2Ckabab%29.jpg/250px-Traditional_Holiday_Lunch_of_Bangladesh%28_Polao_Korma_ilish_vaja%2Ckabab%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Traditional_Holiday_Lunch_of_Bangladesh%28_Polao_Korma_ilish_vaja%2Ckabab%29.jpg/500px-Traditional_Holiday_Lunch_of_Bangladesh%28_Polao_Korma_ilish_vaja%2Ckabab%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a><figcaption> A classic Bangladeshi holiday lunch: plain pilaf served with fried <a href="/wiki/Ilish" title="Ilish">hilsa</a>, kebab, and rich chicken or beef korma.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>, <i>polao</i> (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">পোলাও</span></span>), is a popular ceremonial dish cooked only with aromatic rice. Bangladesh cultivates many varieties of aromatic rice, which can be found only in this country and some surrounding Indian states with predominantly Bengali populations. Historically, there were many varieties of aromatic rice. These included short-grain rice with buttery and other fragrances depending on the variety. Over a long span of time, many recipes were lost and then reinvented.
</p><p>Since the 1970s in Bangladesh <i>pulao</i> has referred to aromatic rice (<span title="Bengali-language text"><span lang="bn">বাসন্তী পোলাও</span></span>) <i>Bashonti polao</i>, first fried either in oil or clarified butter with onions, fresh ginger and whole aromatic spices such as cardamom, cinnamon, black pepper, and more, depending on each household and region. This is then cooked in stock or water, first boiled and then steamed. It is finished off with a bit more clarified butter and fragrant essences such as rose water or kewra water. For presentation, beresta (fried onions) are sprinkled on top. Chicken <i>pulao</i>, (<i>morog pulao</i>) is a traditional ceremonial dish among the Bangladeshi Muslim community. There are several different types of <i>morog pulao</i> found only in particular regions or communities.
</p><p>In Sylhet and Chittagong, a popular ceremonial dish called <i><a href="/wiki/Akhni" title="Akhni">akhni</a> polao</i>. <i>Aqni</i> being the rich stock in which mutton is cooked and then used to cook the rice. Another very spicy <i>Polao</i> dish very popular and unique to Bangladesh is called <i>Tehari</i>. It is very different in taste to the <i>tahris</i> found in some parts of neighboring India. They are most popularly eaten with beef and <i>chevon</i> (goat meat) but are also paired with chicken.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Long2015&#95;46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Long2015-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Young small potatoes, mustard oil (which is alternated with clarified butter or oil depending on individual taste), and a unique spice blend found in <i>teharis</i> distinguish them from other meat <i>polaos</i>. The most famous <i>tehari</i> in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a> is called <i><a href="/wiki/Hajir_biryani" class="mw-redirect" title="Hajir biryani">Hajir biryani</a></i>. Although here the name <i>biryani</i> is a misnomer, in usage among the urban young population it differentiates the popular dish mutton <i>biryanis</i> (goat meat).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Brazil">Brazil</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Brazil"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A significantly modified version of the recipe, often seen as influenced by what is called <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">arroz pilau</i></span> there, is known in <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_cuisine" title="Brazilian cuisine">Brazil</a> as <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">arroz de frango desfiado</i></span> or <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">risoto de frango</i></span> (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991" /><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Portuguese:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="pt-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">&#91;ɐˈʁoz<span class="wrap"> </span>dʒi<span class="wrap"> </span>ˈfɾɐ̃ɡu<span class="wrap"> </span>dʒisfiˈadu&#93;</a></span>, "shredded chicken rice"; <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="pt-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">&#91;ʁiˈzotu&#93;</a></span>, "chicken <a href="/wiki/Risotto" title="Risotto">risotto</a>"). Rice lightly <a href="/wiki/Sofrito" title="Sofrito">fried</a> (and optionally seasoned), salted and cooked until soft (but neither soupy nor sticky) in either water or chicken stock is added to chicken stock, onions and sometimes cubed bell peppers (cooked in the stock), shredded chicken breast, green peas, tomato sauce, <a href="/wiki/Soy_sauce" title="Soy sauce">shoyu</a>, and optionally vegetables (e.g. canned sweet corn, cooked carrot cubes, courgette cubes, <a href="/wiki/Broccolini" title="Broccolini">broccolini</a> flowers, chopped broccoli or broccolini stalks or leaves fried in garlic seasoning) or herbs (e.g., mint, like in <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt"><a href="/wiki/Canja_de_galinha" title="Canja de galinha">canja</a></i></span>) to form a distantly <a href="/wiki/Risotto" title="Risotto">risotto</a>-like dish – but it is generally fluffy (depending on the texture of the rice being added), as generally, once all ingredients are mixed, it is not left to cook longer than five minutes. In the case shredded chicken breast is not added, with the rice being instead served alongside chicken and <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">sauce suprême</i></span>, it is known as <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">arroz suprême de frango</i></span> (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1177148991" /><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Portuguese:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="pt-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">&#91;ɐˈʁos<span class="wrap"> </span>suˈpɾẽm(i)<span class="wrap"> </span>dʒi<span class="wrap"> </span>ˈfɾɐ̃ɡu&#93;</a></span>, "chicken <a href="/wiki/Supreme_(cookery)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme (cookery)">supreme</a> rice").
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Caribbean">Caribbean</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Caribbean"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_cuisine" title="Caribbean cuisine">Caribbean cuisine</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:LiviesFamilyFunDay2018SaltfishAndCallaloo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/LiviesFamilyFunDay2018SaltfishAndCallaloo.jpg/250px-LiviesFamilyFunDay2018SaltfishAndCallaloo.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/LiviesFamilyFunDay2018SaltfishAndCallaloo.jpg/500px-LiviesFamilyFunDay2018SaltfishAndCallaloo.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4048" data-file-height="3036" /></a><figcaption>Caribbean-style <i>pelau</i> with <a href="/wiki/Saltfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltfish">saltfish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Caribbean">Eastern Caribbean</a> and other Caribbean territories there are variations of <i><a href="/wiki/Pelau" title="Pelau">pelau</a></i> which include a wide range of ingredients such as <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon peas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pea" title="Pea">green peas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_bean" title="Green bean">green beans</a>, corn, carrots, pumpkin, and meat such as beef or chicken, or cured pig tail.  The seasoned meat is usually cooked in a stew, with the rice and other vegetables added afterwards. Coconut milk and spices are also key additions in some islands.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">Trinidad</a> is recognized for its <i>pelau</i>, a layered rice with meats and vegetables. It is a mix of traditional <a href="/wiki/African_cuisine" title="African cuisine">African cuisine</a> and "New World" ingredients like <a href="/wiki/Ketchup" title="Ketchup">ketchup</a>. The process of browning the meat (usually chicken, but also stew beef or lamb) in <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> is an African technique.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ganeshram&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ganeshram-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>, <i>pelau</i> is commonly made with <a href="/wiki/Crab_meat" title="Crab meat">crab</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ganeshram&#95;47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ganeshram-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Central_Asia">Central Asia</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Central Asia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Plov_Tashkent.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Plov_Tashkent.jpg/250px-Plov_Tashkent.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Plov_Tashkent.jpg/500px-Plov_Tashkent.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>Restaurant cooking in <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Samarkand_Zigir-pilaf.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Samarkand_Zigir-pilaf.jpg/250px-Samarkand_Zigir-pilaf.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Samarkand_Zigir-pilaf.jpg/500px-Samarkand_Zigir-pilaf.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="5312" data-file-height="2988" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a> pilaf cooked with linseed oil</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_cuisine" title="Central Asian cuisine">Central Asian</a>, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_cuisine" title="Uzbek cuisine">Uzbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_cuisine" title="Kyrgyz cuisine">Kyrgyz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tajik_cuisine" title="Tajik cuisine">Tajik</a> (<a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>: <i lang="uz">Osh, Palov</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>: <span lang="ky">Аш, палоо</span>, <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a>: <span lang="tg">Палов</span>) Kazakh, Turkmen, Karakalpak (<a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>: <span lang="kk">Палау, Palaw</span>) or <i>osh</i> differs from other preparations in that rice is not steamed, but instead <a href="/wiki/Simmer" class="mw-redirect" title="Simmer">simmered</a> in a rich <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stew</a> of meat and vegetables called <i>zirvak</i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%B7%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BA" class="extiw" title="wikt:зирвак">зирвак</a>), until all the liquid is absorbed into the rice. A limited degree of steaming is commonly achieved by covering the pot. It is usually cooked in a <i><a href="/wiki/Kazon_(cookware)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazon (cookware)">kazon</a></i> (or <i>deghi</i>) over an open fire. The cooking tradition includes many regional and occasional variations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-StreetFood&#95;19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StreetFood-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-uzbek&#95;palov&#95;48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uzbek_palov-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Commonly, it is prepared with <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a> or <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, browned in lamb fat or oil, and then stewed with fried <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a> and carrots. <a href="/wiki/Chicken_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicken (food)">Chicken</a> palov is rare but found in traditional recipes originating in <a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a>. Some regional varieties use distinct types of oil to cook the meat. For example, <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a>-style plov commonly uses <i>zig'ir</i> oil, a mix of melon seed, <a href="/wiki/Cottonseed_oil" title="Cottonseed oil">cottonseed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesame_seed" class="mw-redirect" title="Sesame seed">sesame seed</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Linseed_oil" title="Linseed oil">flaxseed</a> oils. Plov is usually simply spiced with salt, <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">peppercorns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cumin" title="Cumin">cumin</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Coriander" title="Coriander">coriander</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barberry" class="mw-redirect" title="Barberry">barberries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peppercorn" class="mw-redirect" title="Peppercorn">red pepper</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Pot_marigold" class="mw-redirect" title="Pot marigold">marigold</a> may be added according to regional variation or the chef's preference. Heads of garlic and chickpeas are sometimes buried into the rice during cooking. Sweet variations with dried <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cranberry" title="Cranberry">cranberries</a> and raisins are prepared on special occasions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Plov is the national dish of <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> and was recognized by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> and inscribed on its <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">Intangible Cultural Heritage of Humanity</a> list in 2016. However neighbouring countries including <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> also considers plov a staple dish, with their own regional variations reflecting local ingredients and cooking.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although often prepared at home, plov is made on special occasions by an <i>oshpaz</i> or <i>ashpoz</i> (osh/ash master chef), who cooks it over an open flame, sometimes serving up to 1,000 people from a single cauldron on holidays or occasions such as weddings. <i>Oshi nahor</i>, or "morning palov", is served in the early morning (between 6 and 9 am) to large gatherings of guests, typically as part of an ongoing wedding celebration.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Uzbek-style plov is found in the post-<a href="/wiki/Soviet_cuisine" title="Soviet cuisine">Soviet</a> countries and <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region</a> of China. In Xinjiang, where the dish is known as polu, polo, or pola (<a href="/wiki/Uyghur_language" title="Uyghur language">Uyghur</a>: <span lang="ug" dir="rtl">پولو، پولۇ، پولا</span>), it is often served with pickled vegetables, including carrots, onion and tomato.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="center gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
	<li class="gallerycaption">Rice pilaf examples from Central Asia</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 210px; height: 175px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Plov122.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Uzbek plov being prepared in a kazon in a Tashkent home"><img alt="Uzbek plov being prepared in a kazon in a Tashkent home" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Plov122.jpg/250px-Plov122.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Plov122.jpg/330px-Plov122.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Plov122.jpg/500px-Plov122.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="786" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext"><a href="/wiki/Uzbek_plov" title="Uzbek plov">Uzbek plov</a> being prepared in a <i><a href="/wiki/Kazon_(cookware)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazon (cookware)">kazon</a></i> in a Tashkent home</div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 210px; height: 175px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Tajik plov, or oshi palav, is a regional variation of pilaf in Tajikistan."><img alt="Tajik plov, or oshi palav, is a regional variation of pilaf in Tajikistan." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg/250px-Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="135" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg/330px-Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg/500px-Oshi_palov_tajik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Tajik plov, or oshi palav, is a regional variation of pilaf in Tajikistan. </div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 210px; height: 175px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Polu.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Uyghur polu"><img alt="Uyghur polu" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Polu.jpg/250px-Polu.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Polu.jpg/330px-Polu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Polu.jpg/500px-Polu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext"><a href="/wiki/Uyghur_cuisine" title="Uyghur cuisine">Uyghur</a> <i>polu</i></div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 210px; height: 175px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajik_plov.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Tajik oshpaz"><img alt="Tajik oshpaz" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Tajik_plov.jpg/120px-Tajik_plov.jpg" decoding="async" width="105" height="145" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Tajik_plov.jpg/250px-Tajik_plov.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1405" data-file-height="1932" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext"><a href="/wiki/Tajik_cuisine" title="Tajik cuisine">Tajik</a> <i>oshpaz</i></div>
		</li>
</ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Greece">Greece</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Greece"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_foods.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Greek_foods.jpg/250px-Greek_foods.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="179" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Greek_foods.jpg/500px-Greek_foods.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1406" data-file-height="1004" /></a><figcaption>A Greek meal with rice pilaf (bottom right)</figcaption></figure>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Greek_cuisine" title="Greek cuisine">Greek cuisine</a>, <i>piláfi</i> (πιλάφι) is fluffy and soft, but neither soupy nor sticky, rice that has been boiled in a meat stock or <a href="/wiki/Bouillon_cube" title="Bouillon cube">bouillon broth</a>. In Northern Greece, it is considered improper to prepare <i>piláfi</i> on a stovetop; the pot is properly placed in the oven.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <i>Gamopílafo</i> ("wedding pilaf") is the prized pilaf served traditionally at weddings and major celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>: rice is boiled in lamb or goat broth, then finished with <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemon</a> juice. Although it bears the name, <i>Gamopílafo</i> is not a pilaf but rather a kind of <a href="/wiki/Risotto" title="Risotto">risotto</a>, with a creamy and not fluffy texture.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="India">India</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: India"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><i>Pulao</i> is usually a mixture of  <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> with vegetables, usually <a href="/wiki/Pea" title="Pea">peas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_bean" title="Green bean">green beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrots</a> and sometimes includes any one kind of meat like <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> or <a href="/wiki/Prawn" title="Prawn">prawns</a>. A typical <a href="/wiki/Bengali_cuisine" title="Bengali cuisine">Bengali</a> style pulao is prepared using vegetarian ingredients like <a href="/wiki/Long-grain_rice" class="mw-redirect" title="Long-grain rice">Long grain rice</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aromatic_rice" title="Aromatic rice">aromatic rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cashewnut" class="mw-redirect" title="Cashewnut">cashewnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raisin" title="Raisin">raisin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghee" title="Ghee">ghee</a> and various spices like <a href="/wiki/Nutmeg" title="Nutmeg">nutmeg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_leaf" title="Bay leaf">bay leaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinnamon" title="Cinnamon">cinnamon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cumin" title="Cumin">cumin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clove" title="Clove">clove</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mace_(spice)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mace (spice)">mace</a>. There are also a few very elaborate <i>pulaos</i> with Persian names like <i>hazar pasand</i> ("a thousand delights").<sup id="cite&#95;ref-FOOTNOTEDavidson2014&#95;54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavidson2014-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is usually served on special occasions and weddings, though it is not uncommon to eat it for a regular lunch or dinner meal. It is considered very high in <a href="/wiki/Food_energy" title="Food energy">food energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fat</a>. A pulao is often complemented with either spiced yogurt or <i><a href="/wiki/Raita" title="Raita">raita</a></i>.
</p>
<ul class="center gallery mw-gallery-packed">
	<li class="gallerycaption">Rice pilaf examples from India</li>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Iran">Iran</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Iran"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Loobia_Polo.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Loobia_Polo.jpg/250px-Loobia_Polo.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Loobia_Polo.jpg/500px-Loobia_Polo.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="4197" data-file-height="2778" /></a><figcaption><i>Lubia polo</i>, 'Persian rice with green beans' in Iran</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Persian_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian cuisine">Persian</a> culinary terms referring to <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> preparation are numerous and ancient and have influenced and found their way into the neighbouring languages: <i>polow</i> (from which the word "pilaf" is derived around the world; rice cooked in broth while the grains remain separate, straining the half cooked rice before adding the broth and then "brewing"), <i>chelow</i> (white rice with separate grains), <i><a href="/wiki/Kateh" title="Kateh">kateh</a></i> (sticky rice) and <i><a href="/wiki/Tahchin" title="Tahchin">tahchin</a></i> (slow cooked rice, vegetables, and meat cooked in a specially designed dish). One of the many unique ingredients used in Persian rice is saffron. There are a wide variety of Persian rice dishes (upto 100 dishes) with vegetables and herbs which are very popular among Iranians.  
</p><p>There are four primary methods of cooking rice in Iran:
</p>
<ul><li><i>Chelow</i>: rice that is carefully prepared through soaking and <a href="/wiki/Parboiling" title="Parboiling">parboiling</a>, at which point the water is drained and the rice is steamed. This method results in an exceptionally fluffy rice with the grains separated and not sticky; it also results in a golden rice crust at the bottom of the pot called <i><a href="/wiki/Tahdig" class="mw-redirect" title="Tahdig">tahdig</a></i> (literally "bottom of the pot").</li>
<li><i>Polow</i>: rice that is cooked exactly the same as <i>chelo</i>, with the exception that after draining the rice, other ingredients are layered with the rice, and they are then steamed together.</li>
<li><i>Kateh</i>: rice that is boiled until the water is absorbed. This is the traditional dish of Northern Iran.</li>
<li><i>Dami:</i> Cooked almost the same as <i>kateh</i>, except that the heat is reduced just before boiling and a towel is placed between the lid and the pot to prevent steam from escaping. <i>Dami</i> literally means "simmered".</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Japan">Japan</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Japan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Japanese style Pilaf (ピラフ) is commonly eaten with Japanese school lunch, or kyūshoku (給食). The most common pilaf enjoyed with Japanese school lunch is a corn pilaf.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Kenya">Kenya</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Kenya"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> pilau is mostly eaten in coastal regions. The spices are similar to Indian varieties. Potatoes are typically added to the masala and the dish can be eaten with meat, fish or meatless. It is often served with a side of <a href="/wiki/Kachumbari" title="Kachumbari">kachumbari</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pakistan">Pakistan</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Pakistan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Zafrani_Pulao.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Zafrani_Pulao.jpg/250px-Zafrani_Pulao.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="253" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Zafrani_Pulao.jpg/330px-Zafrani_Pulao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Zafrani_Pulao.jpg/500px-Zafrani_Pulao.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3120" data-file-height="4160" /></a><figcaption>Zafrani chicken pulao, Karachi, Pakistan</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cholistani_Camel_Meat_Pulao.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cholistani_Camel_Meat_Pulao.JPG/250px-Cholistani_Camel_Meat_Pulao.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cholistani_Camel_Meat_Pulao.JPG/500px-Cholistani_Camel_Meat_Pulao.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a><figcaption>Camel meat pulao, Pakistan</figcaption></figure>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <i>pulao</i> (<span title="Urdu-language text"><span lang="ur"><span class="Nastaliq" dir="rtl" title="Nastaliq" style="font-family: &#39;Jameel Noori Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Urdu Typesetting&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu&#39;, &#39;Noto Nastaliq Urdu Draft&#39;, &#39;Hussaini Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;AlQalam Taj Nastaleeq&#39;, IranNastaliq, &#39;Awami Nastaliq&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta3&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta2&#39;, &#39;Awami Nastaliq Beta1&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;Nafees Nastaleeq v1.01&#39;, &#39;Pak Nastaleeq&#39;, &#39;PDMS&#95;Jauhar&#39;, &#39;Alvi Lahori Nastaleeq&#39;; font-size: 110%; font-style: normal;">پلاؤ</span></span></span>), also romanized as <i><span title="Urdu-language text"><i lang="ur-Latn">pulāv</i></span></i><b>,</b> is a popular dish made with fragrant <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">basmati</a> rice cooked in a seasoned meat or bone broth. Typically non-spicy, it features tender pieces of meat, such as chicken, lamb, or beef, though vegetarian variations are also popular. As with Afghan cuisine, <i><a href="/wiki/Kabuli_palaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabuli palaw">Kabuli pulav</a></i> is a staple dish in Pakistan, especially in the western regions. This variation of pulav is often adorned with sliced carrots, almonds, and raisins fried in a sweet syrup, adding a unique touch of sweetness and texture to the dish.
<a href="/wiki/Bannu" title="Bannu">Bannu Beef Pulao</a>, also known as Bannu Gosht Pulao, is a traditional and popular variation of pulav recipe hailing from the <a href="/wiki/Bannu_District" title="Bannu District">Bannu district</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa" title="Khyber Pakhtunkhwa">Khyber Pakhtunkhwa</a> province in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>. The dish is made with beef, basmati rice, and a blend of local spices, resulting in a flavor profile characteristic of the region. The beef is first cooked in a separate preparation known as <a href="/wiki/Yahni" title="Yahni">Beef Yakhni</a>, made using a combination of salt, ginger, garlic, onions, and garam masala. This broth enhances the flavor and ensures the meat is tender. The rice is then combined with the cooked beef, allowing the flavors to meld together. This delicacy is often served during special occasions and family dinners and is a <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">Pashtun</a> culinary tradition.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Pulao is popular in all parts of Pakistan, but the cooking style can vary slightly in other parts of the country. It is prepared by <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Sindhi people">Sindhi people</a> of Pakistan in their marriage ceremonies, condolence meetings, and other occasions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Romania">Romania</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Romania"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Romanian style <i>pilaf</i> is often more watery in consistency, more akin to <a href="/wiki/Congee" title="Congee">congee</a>, and uses chicken breast meat along with chopped red peppers, onion, and carrot.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Levant">Levant</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Levant"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Traditional Levantine cooking includes a variety of Pilaf known as "<a href="/wiki/Maqlubeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Maqlubeh">Maqlubeh</a>", known across the countries of the Eastern Mediterranean.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The rice pilaf which is traditionally cooked with meat, eggplant, tomatoes, potatoes, and cauliflower also has a fish variety known as "<a href="/wiki/Sayadieh" title="Sayadieh">sayadieh</a>", or the Fishermen's Dish.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Turkey">Turkey</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Turkey"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pilav.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Pilav.JPG/250px-Pilav.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Pilav.JPG/500px-Pilav.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption>Typical Turkish pilav. Rice with <a href="/wiki/Orzo_(pasta)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orzo (pasta)">orzo</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Historically, mutton stock was the most common cooking liquid for Turkish pilavs.
</p><p>Turkish cuisine contains many different pilav types. Some of these variations are <i>pirinç</i> (rice) pilav, <i><a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">bulgur</a></i> pilav, and <i>arpa şehriye</i> (<a href="/wiki/Orzo" title="Orzo">orzo</a>) pilav. Using mainly these three types, Turkish people make many dishes such as <i><a href="/wiki/Perdeli_pilav" title="Perdeli pilav">perdeli pilav</a></i>, and <i>etli pilav</i> (rice cooked with cubed beef). Unlike Chinese rice, if Turkish rice is sticky, it is considered unsuccessful. To make the best rice according to Turkish people, one must rinse the rice, cook in butter, then add the water and let it sit until it soaks all the water. This results in a pilaf that is not sticky and every single rice grain falls off of the spoon separately.
</p><p>The Greek Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Greeks" title="Pontic Greeks">Pontian</a> minority had their own methods of preparing pilav.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pontians along the Black Sea coast might make pilav with anchovies (called <span title="Pontic-language text"><i lang="pnt">hapsipilavon</i></span>) or mussels (called <span title="Pontic-language text"><i lang="pnt">mythopilavon</i></span>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other varieties of Pontian pilav could include chicken,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> lamb, and vegetables. Typical seasonings are anise, dill, parsley, salt, pepper, and saffron. Some Pontians cooked pine nuts, peanuts, or almonds into their pilav. While pilav was usually made from rice, it could also be made with buckwheat.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Crimea">Crimea</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Crimea"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_cuisine" title="Crimean Tatar cuisine">Crimean Tatar pilyav</a> (pilâv) is prepared from rice; meat, onions, or raisins can be added.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Baltics">Baltics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pilaf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Baltics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Lithuanian pilaf is often referred to as <i>plovas</i>. It tends to consist of rice and vegetables; depending on the region the vegetables can be tomatoes, carrots, cabbage, and/or mushrooms. It often contains chicken pieces or cut-up pieces of pork, usually the meat around the neck or the stomach; seasonings can be heavy or light, and some <i>plovas</i> might be made with rice that is very soft, unlike other variants.
</p><p>Latvian pilaf is often referred to as <i>plovs</i> or <i>plov</i>. It tends to contain the same ingredients as the Lithuanian <i>plovas</i> and can vary from county to county.
</p>

<li id="cite&#95;note-StreetFood-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-StreetFood_19-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-StreetFood_19-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Bruce Kraig, Colleen Taylor Sen. <i>Street Food Around the World: An Encyclopedia of Food and Culture</i>. <li id="cite&#95;note-KTAchaya1994-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-KTAchaya1994_25-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFK.&#95;T.&#95;Achaya1994" class="citation book cs1"><a href="/wiki/K._T._Achaya" title="K. T. Achaya">K. T. Achaya</a> (1994). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=-cFcH2ZHWLcC"><i>Indian food: a historical companion</i></a>. Oxford University Press. p.&#160;11. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-562845-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-19-562845-6"><bdi>978-0-19-562845-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Indian+food%3A+a+historical+companion&amp;rft.pages=11&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-19-562845-6&amp;rft.au=K.+T.+Achaya&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D-cFcH2ZHWLcC&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APilaf" class="Z3988"></span></span>
